     513             :    8: DECL_DECLARED_CONSTEXPR_P (in VAR_DECL, FUNCTION_DECL)
     514             : 
     515             :    Usage of language-independent fields in a language-dependent manner:
     516             : 
     517             :    TYPE_ALIAS_SET
     518             :      This field is used by TYPENAME_TYPEs, TEMPLATE_TYPE_PARMs, and so
     519             :      forth as a substitute for the mark bits provided in `lang_type'.
     520             :      At present, only the six low-order bits are used.
     521             : 
     522             :    TYPE_LANG_SLOT_1
     523             :      For a FUNCTION_TYPE or METHOD_TYPE, this is TYPE_RAISES_EXCEPTIONS.
     524             :      For a POINTER_TYPE (to a METHOD_TYPE), this is TYPE_PTRMEMFUNC_TYPE.
     525             :      For an ENUMERAL_TYPE, BOUND_TEMPLATE_TEMPLATE_PARM_TYPE,
     526             :      RECORD_TYPE or UNION_TYPE this is TYPE_TEMPLATE_INFO,
     527             : 
     528             :   BINFO_VIRTUALS
     529             :      For a binfo, this is a TREE_LIST.  There is an entry for each
     530             :      virtual function declared either in BINFO or its direct and
     531             :      indirect primary bases.
     532             : 
     533             :      The BV_DELTA of each node gives the amount by which to adjust the
     534             :      `this' pointer when calling the function.  If the method is an
     535             :      overridden version of a base class method, then it is assumed
     536             :      that, prior to adjustment, the this pointer points to an object
     537             :      of the base class.
     538             : 
     539             :      The BV_VCALL_INDEX of each node, if non-NULL, gives the vtable
     540             :      index of the vcall offset for this entry.
     541             : 
     542             :      The BV_FN is the declaration for the virtual function itself.
     543             : 
     544             :      If BV_LOST_PRIMARY is set, it means that this entry is for a lost
     545             :      primary virtual base and can be left null in the vtable.
     546             : 
     547             :    BINFO_VTABLE
     548             :      This is an expression with POINTER_TYPE that gives the value
     549             :      to which the vptr should be initialized.  Use get_vtbl_decl_for_binfo
     550             :      to extract the VAR_DECL for the complete vtable.
     551             : 
     552             :    DECL_VINDEX
     553             :      This field is NULL for a non-virtual function.  For a virtual
     554             :      function, it is eventually set to an INTEGER_CST indicating the
     555             :      index in the vtable at which this function can be found.  When
     556             :      a virtual function is declared, but before it is known what
     557             :      function is overridden, this field is the error_mark_node.
     558             : 
     559             :      Temporarily, it may be set to a TREE_LIST whose TREE_VALUE is
     560             :      the virtual function this one overrides, and whose TREE_CHAIN is
     561             :      the old DECL_VINDEX.  */
     562             :

    1993             : 
    1994             : /* This structure provides additional information above and beyond
    1995             :    what is provide in the ordinary tree_type.  In the past, we used it
    1996             :    for the types of class types, template parameters types, typename
    1997             :    types, and so forth.  However, there can be many (tens to hundreds
    1998             :    of thousands) of template parameter types in a compilation, and
    1999             :    there's no need for this additional information in that case.
    2000             :    Therefore, we now use this data structure only for class types.
    2001             : 
    2002             :    In the past, it was thought that there would be relatively few
    2003             :    class types.  However, in the presence of heavy use of templates,
    2004             :    many (i.e., thousands) of classes can easily be generated.
    2005             :    Therefore, we should endeavor to keep the size of this structure to
    2006             :    a minimum.  */

    4775             : 
    4776             : /* A thunk is a stub function.
    4777             : 
    4778             :    A thunk is an alternate entry point for an ordinary FUNCTION_DECL.
    4779             :    The address of the ordinary FUNCTION_DECL is given by the
    4780             :    DECL_INITIAL, which is always an ADDR_EXPR whose operand is a
    4781             :    FUNCTION_DECL.  The job of the thunk is to either adjust the this
    4782             :    pointer before transferring control to the FUNCTION_DECL, or call
    4783             :    FUNCTION_DECL and then adjust the result value. Note, the result
    4784             :    pointer adjusting thunk must perform a call to the thunked
    4785             :    function, (or be implemented via passing some invisible parameter
    4786             :    to the thunked function, which is modified to perform the
    4787             :    adjustment just before returning).
    4788             : 
    4789             :    A thunk may perform either, or both, of the following operations:
    4790             : 
    4791             :    o Adjust the this or result pointer by a constant offset.
    4792             :    o Adjust the this or result pointer by looking up a vcall or vbase offset
    4793             :      in the vtable.
    4794             : 
    4795             :    A this pointer adjusting thunk converts from a base to a derived
    4796             :    class, and hence adds the offsets. A result pointer adjusting thunk
    4797             :    converts from a derived class to a base, and hence subtracts the
    4798             :    offsets.  If both operations are performed, then the constant
    4799             :    adjustment is performed first for this pointer adjustment and last
    4800             :    for the result pointer adjustment.
    4801             : 
    4802             :    The constant adjustment is given by THUNK_FIXED_OFFSET.  If the
    4803             :    vcall or vbase offset is required, THUNK_VIRTUAL_OFFSET is
    4804             :    used. For this pointer adjusting thunks, it is the vcall offset
    4805             :    into the vtable.  For result pointer adjusting thunks it is the
    4806             :    binfo of the virtual base to convert to.  Use that binfo's vbase
    4807             :    offset.
    4808             : 
    4809             :    It is possible to have equivalent covariant thunks.  These are
    4810             :    distinct virtual covariant thunks whose vbase offsets happen to
    4811             :    have the same value.  THUNK_ALIAS is used to pick one as the
    4812             :    canonical thunk, which will get all the this pointer adjusting
    4813             :    thunks attached to it.  */
    4814             : 
    4815             : /* An integer indicating how many bytes should be subtracted from the
    4816             :    this or result pointer when this function is called.  */
    4817             : #define THUNK_FIXED_OFFSET(DECL) \
    4818             :   (DECL_LANG_SPECIFIC (THUNK_FUNCTION_CHECK (DECL))->u.fn.u5.fixed_offset)
    4819             : 
    4820             : /* A tree indicating how to perform the virtual adjustment. For a this
    4821             :    adjusting thunk it is the number of bytes to be added to the vtable
    4822             :    to find the vcall offset. For a result adjusting thunk, it is the
    4823             :    binfo of the relevant virtual base.  If NULL, then there is no
    4824             :    virtual adjust.  (The vptr is always located at offset zero from
    4825             :    the this or result pointer.)  (If the covariant type is within the
    4826             :    class hierarchy being laid out, the vbase index is not yet known
    4827             :    at the point we need to create the thunks, hence the need to use
    4828             :    binfos.)  */
    4829             : 
    4830             : #define THUNK_VIRTUAL_OFFSET(DECL) \
    4831             :   (LANG_DECL_U2_CHECK (FUNCTION_DECL_CHECK (DECL), 0)->access)
    4832             : 
    4833             : /* A thunk which is equivalent to another thunk.  */

    5068             :       A name is said to have linkage when it might denote the same

    5071             :

    5540             : /* These constants can used as bit flags in the process of tree formatting.

    5542             :    TFF_PLAIN_IDENTIFIER: unqualified part of a name.
    5543             :    TFF_SCOPE: include the class and namespace scope of the name.
    5544             :    TFF_CHASE_TYPEDEF: print the original type-id instead of the typedef-name.
    5545             :    TFF_DECL_SPECIFIERS: print decl-specifiers.
    5546             :    TFF_CLASS_KEY_OR_ENUM: precede a class-type name (resp. enum name) with
    5547             :        a class-key (resp. `enum').
    5548             :    TFF_RETURN_TYPE: include function return type.
    5549             :    TFF_FUNCTION_DEFAULT_ARGUMENTS: include function default parameter values.
    5550             :    TFF_EXCEPTION_SPECIFICATION: show function exception specification.
    5551             :    TFF_TEMPLATE_HEADER: show the template<...> header in a
    5552             :        template-declaration.
    5553             :    TFF_TEMPLATE_NAME: show only template-name.
    5554             :    TFF_EXPR_IN_PARENS: parenthesize expressions.
    5555             :    TFF_NO_FUNCTION_ARGUMENTS: don't show function arguments.
    5556             :    TFF_UNQUALIFIED_NAME: do not print the qualifying scope of the
    5557             :        top-level entity.
    5558             :    TFF_NO_OMIT_DEFAULT_TEMPLATE_ARGUMENTS: do not omit template arguments
    5559             :        identical to their defaults.
    5560             :    TFF_NO_TEMPLATE_BINDINGS: do not print information about the template
    5561             :        arguments for a function template specialization.
